Of the destillinge of honey* we have written before amongst the waters that
be destilled in Roosestilles. c. The last liquor that runs here out, is
somewhat thick, (that I judge,) it may be called an oil.

Oils destilled may also be mixte together one with an oteer, as in this
medicine of Epiphanius Empiricus, praised for frakens and all kind of
ruggedness and spots of the face. An ounce and a half of virgins milcke.
Water of Rooses with a little brimstone, an ounce. Oils of Tartaro, of wheat,
of yelkes or Eggs, of every one half an ounce: a scrupul of Caphurae.
Although the seoyles are not wont to be made by destillacion: yet oil of
wheat and of the yelkes of eggs, are better made destilled.

Of oils of metals, tile stones, Gagate, Aumber.
WAters and oils, secret by the singular Syluius. This virtue of pearsinge
seems to pertain chieflye unto oils drawn out of metalles, in the which
also is a greater force

I understand that Vinegar is chieflye used to be destild, for the drawing out
of oils out of Metalies, as Antimoni, Lead, Cerussa. Other use other sharp
and most hot liquors for that purpose, as sharply, burning water, urine
destilled, Aqua Forti.

Lullius in the fifth Canon of his first book of quintessence, when he had
taught to draw out the.iiii. elements out of plants, he added. And make
them to resolve with our Menstrue (I suppose he means our Urine) under
dounge for the space of a weke: the Menstruum must be sharp with some Vegetable
and strong quickenynge things which we shall declare hereafter in the
Questionary. After the metalles shall be dissolved set them to be destilled in
a fire of the first degree, and the Menstruum shall issue forth, and the lime
or powder of ye metal shall remain in the bottom. After this reiterat repeat
it again upon the dregs Menstruum as much as the weight of the metal, and set
it to putrifyinge for the space of a month and a half: and after this destill
it as thou did of the Vegetable or quickening things, but every time put new
Menstruum upon the dregs. Other diverse opinions of Philosophers in the drawing
out of the elements out of mineral things, we shall declare in the third
book: This saith he.

I suppose it to be a commone thing unto all Cardanus signifieih and an other
certain author writes, that the drops oil of Vitriol or Coproos to be
ponderous and weighty.

Oil destilled of Orpment or Mysi (or Vitriol of Rom.) anointed upon ye
arteries region of the hart, I suppose is hable to save a ma infected with
poison, be it never so sharp and strong, do kill a manne only with touching:
Cardanus.

And a little after, but sense we are fallen into nor far fro the purpose to
inquere this how oil may be made which being anointed upon the Arteriis,
makes the venom to break out by vomit or purgation, or sweat, or urine, It
is sure, it must be of metal, which must be most strong. I saw such once
and by the waighte only I conjectured that it was without al dout of metal,
It must also be of the nature of Venom: for by the immoderate heate, as it
is said, it vanquishes first the evil infection conceived Laser or Assa
Foeetida. Therefore those things that must drive out the poysone, ought to be
metally poisons, but not most bitter: and most hot and discussing or expelling,
also in a manner contrary to the poisons. The matter therefore Mysi Orpment, and
the juice of Laser or Assa foetida, and Gentian, and of the fat of venomous
serpents, and Aconitum. If so be it that in any land moo of these (foresaid
virtues, as to discus, expel, and resist poysones. c. be to be gotten, the
oil extracted by the force of fire shall be best of all. And a little after.
But oil that only by anoyntinge of the Arteries doth thrust out the
poysone, I would not call it the best in this sense drink, Triacle or Milk
or sum other excellent medicin, ye also it should be the more auaylable. That
dare I be bold to say, that the anointing of the arteries, and the things
ministered outwardly, are better and of more strength then those things that are
drunk, save only for this that the poison remains yet in the stomach. For
unto such (poisons newly taken, that they be not yet gone out of the stomach)
they that provoke strong vomities are most excellent, as Milk, Lie, Oyll,
water of Nucis vomicae or spewing nut. Therefore in venomous bytinges, in
stingings in oyntmentes that be venomous, in the drinking of venom which is
now already pierced to the midriff or nether parts of the chest, the helps that
be ministered outwardly are more available and of greater strength. c. This out
of Cardane have I written the more at large, that thereby also ye reason migth
be the more evident of that marvelous oil of Scorpions. c. Which because it
is made without destillacion,

Oyll of Antimonium is most proffitable to all ill soores and boils, as I my
self dotry with good success. But the Antimonium is purged first, oftetimes
melted and made liquid with the fire. Far from this doth the oyll of Antimonium
which chymistes use, wherewithal they endeavour to set the colour of gould upon
silver: Matthaeolus upon Diosc.

Oyll of Antimonium howe it is made for soore boils and fistulas. I writ before
out of Vlstadius, Quintessence. But certain practicioners also make oyll of
Antimonium to diverse diseases within the body, which they extol with
marvelous and great praises. They make it after this sort, as I here. Antimonii
half a pound, whyt Tartari Calcionated as much: let the be beaten and melted
or dissolved in a gouldsmithes Tigillo (crucibulo) upon cools: when they are
melted let them be powered out into sum earthen pot, where they shall be stirred
and mixed together: and when they are becum into a hard lump, let them Hyppocras
as they call it) in a moist place (in a hoot and moist place) as in a wine
cellar, the colender hanging: for so shall the oyll destill out by little little
which of sum because of the bloody colour is called Rubedo Antimanii, and
likewise it is made of certain Gouldsmithes for a certain painting I can not
tell what. But for the remedies of mans body it ought to be prepared with
Quintessence of wyn Antimonium: and let them be sturde diligently in body, and
mixed, and then destilled in ashes three or iiii. times, till the breath lose al
the evil smell. The dregs must always be mixed stirred about when you powrest i^
again the destilled water upon the, or when thou powrest to them new
Quintessence, for I am not sure which way it ought to be done. Sum in the
beginning do stregthway mixed reed Antimoniu Tartaru calcionated to be melted
together. But I wryt althies not as certain: but as I noted the by the way as I
hard them recited certain years ago of a certain practicioner. I know that
certain chymistes goldsmiths search for ye oil or Quint essence of ye
Antimoniu as a most perfect treasur. This destil first sharp lye composed of
vnslect lyme and ashes Clauellatas by a Filtru: and is this lye they sis the
Antimoniu subtly and fynly beten, for the space of.v. hours, and again
destil this lye when it is cold, by a Filtru: that of ye Antimoniu Antimoniu
put in a Cucurbita or body, most sharpe red vinegar destilled, so that it be
above it iii. or.iiii. fingars thick: they set it in a hoot place a few days,
and every day they shake and* mixed it, x. or.xx. times: then they power ye
vinegar lightly into an other glass, so yt nothing be troubled. This do ^hey
repeat.v. or.vi. times (ever pouring new vinegar upon the Antimoniu remaining
in ye Cucurbita quintessence of Antimoniu, is of a colour of blud. With this
they die Mercurie, say it is an incomparable treasure, a chief mystery of ye
chymistical art: as we traslated out of a certain written doutch book. A reed
oyll is gotten out of Antimoniu, very sharp, smelling lyk brimston, it
retains ye virtue of y^ Antiminium, because of the grosnes of the substance
proffitable Cardanus.

Hooll Lyme vnbroken, let it be slekt in comun oyll, and destill it in a
lembeck of glass, there shall issue forth an oyll good for a boon that is
corrupt: Syluius. Put a hot piece of quick Lyme into commun oyll, till the Lyme
becum powder, then let it be destilled in a lembeck of glass, and oyll of Lyme
shall issue, which is the first that was described by Leonard of Praedapalea
Patauinus, Ion. Iacobus de Manliis.

Oyll of Cerussa: Look before where we intreted of Quintessence out of
Vlstadius.

Oyll of Gagates or ieet, called Sacratum or holy, most holsum for them that
be possessed of spirits, that have the falling sickness, the palsy, the cramp,
the stifnes of sinews, the gout, or be chooked in their womb, it helps also
coceiuing. It is made of Ieet stones after the manner of oyll of Juniper (by
descention) or else by sublimacion (as oyll of tyle stones) Mesues of Iac.
Syluius interpretation: out of whose notes we have subscribed this words:
Seeing Bitumen is far lighter cost then Ieet, Bitumen, forasmuch as it is as it
were the fat of the earth, and is burned in steed of oyll of them that dwell
about the place of Asphaltita or deed sea, or else in other places where Bitumen
is. Forthermore he doubts whether it can heel the falling sickness, seeing the
falling sickness doth the more appear with ye foul stinking, smell of the
Bitumen. But me thinks it with it by attenuating, digesting, drying, which
virtues boothe it has them befoore, and that not feablelye: and also much
moore the liquor destilled thereof performs these things.

Nether doth it not help this diese therefore, because it is likely that the same
should be uttered and appear with the perfume of that bituminous smell, as with
the perfume of Myrrh, Galbanum, and horns, houfs, and the skins of a she or he
got. For Phisicions use the horns houfes of diverse bestes Bitumen) specially
white, holden to the nostrils of one sick of the falling evil, with coals in a
spoon and the Amber upon them, and by by Mosch or Ambra will do also. But that
Mesuae writes of men possessed with devils (saith Syluius) is superstitious,
against the faith of a Christen man. Brimston and jet are molten at the fire as
al other liquors. The same.

Oil of philosophers (which some have named oil of wisdom, and of perfect
mastership, divine and holy) by al the old writers consent, is most effectuous
to secret diseases, and tha^ not to a few means of the subtelnes of the
substance, it digests and consumes al excremental and superfluous expelled
matter. Therefore it is very wholesome for the falling sickness, palsy, turning
sickness, for getfulnes, and for the cold diseases of the spleen, rains,
bladder, womb, sinews, al joints, other sinewy parts. But one sort is natural
or mineral and an other of the sea, that runs out of Isles rocks (called
Naphtha) of the which kind, that which is somewhat white is counted the best:
the (alchichil) or old claret, as much as is possible let them sok in the oil.
Dry them by the selves in cases (caczobis. The Munks upon Mesuen: where also is
red shortly after, Caczola for a Cucurbita or body of a Bulcasis) which stopped
very exactly, set it up keep it: for the elder it is the stronger: Mesue as
Syluius traslateth him, whose words also I have written here out of his
annotacios. Oil (saith he) of tiles is so subtle, that more subtle, more hot
and more effectuous in cold diseases, the is oil of balm. It provokes vrin, it
breaks the stone, kills worms: it is holsom for the singing of the ears
coming of a gros wind for the palsi, the crap (spasmo cynico) the sciatica or
ach in the hukle bones, the gout in the knees, fete the greues of the other
joints, being drunk or anointed upon ye place: but let it be drunk mixte with a
little portion of some water convenient for the disease. The making of this oil
is described also Rasis in his Antidotari or preservative and by Bulcasis in
his book entitled Servitor: whereas Bulcasis prefers new tiles, yt never yet
touched water, because they drink in ye oil better: he bids divide the into
pieces of an inch bigness, putreth the so in a vessel of glass, or glased, well
claied yt the third part thereof remain empty. The fire must be made soft at ye
first, but so yt it touch ye bottom, encresed by little little. First shall a
water issue forth afterward an oil (read Bulcasis) which must be gathered
guaiacu many other things. Oil also of Chamaemel, Nard also, which is called
Benet or blessed of Mesuae: but this (of tiles) is ye chief, of so is called
petroleu or oil of stones. These Sylu. This is a stinking oil, but it pierces
passingli. Io. Iac. de Maliis. Read certain things before, where we have entreted
generally of ye destillatio of oils by descecion, out of Vlst. Bull. bids to
dip in the pieces every one of an i^che bigness (a dram, Rasis) made red
hot, in most old oil, and when they are quenched to take them out of y^
oil and when they are al sowhat gross beaten, to put them into one or mo
stillatory vessels: which he calls belies, so that.ii. parts of ye vessel
or more be filled. He bids also to take heed that ye fire come not nie to
this oil (while it is destilled) because it will easily be set on fire, and
hardly be put out. Afterward again new pieces of tiles, dressed as before, to be
destilled, till oil enough be gathered: which he bids to be kept in a vessel
with a narow mouth: most diligently stopte with wax Rasis describe.

The oil that they cal commonly Balsamyn (of spik) raises up sodely them that
lie in the falling Alexander Benet.

This oil is made also with certain other things mixed with it, as I found in a
certain written book, the words whereof I will rehers here. Take break into little
pieces red tiles very old or new, but yt never touched water, they being made
red hot quech them in oil of olives, or else, y^ is better, in oil of bays, by
by make the red hot again, theiwer queshed, if any of it be left, if not, put
new unto it to the measur of a fingar. Afterward put to it Castorei, and
Spicknard, or in the steed of it few, of ether of them one part: Costi two
parts. When this are punned, mixed them with the tiles in a Cucurbita or belly,
which thou shalt dig in horse dong about. rx. days. At length thou shalt
destill it, increasing the fire by little and little. The first liquor is good,
the second better, but the third of a red colour is best. This oyll is good
against Cynical Cramp, being anointed thereupon or drunk, also the Sciatica,
the griefs Ammoniack, dissolveth in short space the impostumes and hardnesses
of the splien. It is of force against the falling sickness and the obstruction
or stopping of the nose, being put into ye noosthrilles. It heats the brain,
confirms the memory, asswageth touth ache. Being put into ye womb, it
provokes the flowers. It brings out the child newly conceived ether dead or
alive. It opens the mouth of the veins, dissolveth the lunges from gros
humours. A few drops of it drunken with syrop of Rooses, helps them that
draw their breeth peinfully. It consumes marvelously the water descending
down to the eyes, that is to say the disease called Suffusion. If fishers
anoint their nets therewith, they shall entyse innumerable fishes. Iron
moystened therein and put to the fire shall burn streigth way. It kills
wornes whersoeuer they be. Being made hoot in an egg shell or other vessel,
may be dropped Rasis in Antidotary attribute and Benet, that is, that which is
destilled of only tiles oil. That is couted the best (saith Rasis) that is very
red, of a strong smell, and of a subtle substance.

Oil of lead: Loke before, whereas we have reher sed Vlstadius words of
Quinessence.

Amber by an artificial means of siething is turned into an oil of his oun
colour. Ge. Agricola In died it is possible to make oil of Amber, after the
same manner as of Jet, whereof we have written The Germains call them by a comun
name Agstein, giving only the difference of black unto Jet. Cardan supposes
that Camphora also is of ye same kind, only because yt this, that the perfume
of Amber received in a moist cloth, gives afterward the smell of Camphora in
it: which notwithstanding did not appear so to me as I did prove it for a
trial.

Brimston anointed druck takes away scabbednes, leprosy and the french
pockes. But with Card. But his books of ye french disease, I suppose are not
yet cum forth in print. Salt coteineth an oyll in it if it be mixed with the lyme
or clay called Bitumen. Wherupo Arrianus declares, amongst the Ichthiophagi,
the men that live only by fyshe, in his history of Ind, howe they make an oyll
of salt. That may be an argument also that the Olive tries delyte in the Sea
Bitume mixed with it. Car.

For the making of oil of Brimston, a ma must chose out yt which is pure never
touched the fire, chiefly alive of an ashy colour.) This oil is made many ways
at Rome, by sublymacio descecion. c. It is good for many things, chiefly for
fistulas, for ye healing of ye wheels of ye moutes excells most of all. For
take and wet the end of a feather or other like thing, as some young and tender
spring of a try or herb, and touche the wheels once or twyse only therewith,
and by and by they shall be killed healed. The Munkes upon Mesue.

Take a vessel of glass (as Maithaeolus Senen. writes in his book of the
French evil) not much unlike to a little bell, daubed with potters clay, hang
it the space of a cubit from the ground, by a wire of bras or iron, under ye
which thou shalt set

Brimstone that never came ny the fire, or most yelowe, while it is brent,
gives a thick smoke to be received in a bell of glass or of stoone. Wherein
thorough the gros vapour an oyll gathered together destilleth into a large plain
vessel, in ye midst whereof the brimstone builded upon a little vessel is brent.
Other beating the brimstone consume the fyry substance of if, with Aqua vitae
set on fire, and after devil that which remains, like unto oyll of
Philosophers. Other sis yelowe Brimstone pound, with a slow fire, with.ii.
vnces of odoriferous wine, till the wine be consumed, (as it is red in Luminari
maiore.) Syluius.

Put one part of quick brimston into.ii. parts parts of oil of Lynsied, beat
them well and diligently together, and let them stand in horse dong ii. dais in
a vessel well shut, it shall be clear fair.

But all these oils seem to be prepared only for this purpose that they may be
ministered without the body: I here say that there be certain practicioners
Syluius makes mention, is first consumed by Aqua vitae set on fire, then
destild by sublimacion, it may be more safely ministered with in the body then
the other.

Oil of Vitriol or copros is desired of chemists and likewise of physicians,
and as a most secrete matter is hid. I will put here some descriptions

Make the Vitriol in to lime, as thou know, then pour burning water unto it,
so that it exceed the Vitriol a little: then seperate the burning water by
destillacion in a phiall or in a crooked still, or out, urge the spirits of the
Vitriol by little and little, increasing the fire more and more, till al ye
spirits be over passed. This liquor destilled put it again into some one of
the.iii. manner of vessels aforsaid, destil it in a kettle full of water, until
whatso ever watery thing is in it, be separated, which thou shalt endeavour to
bring to pas by al the wit thou hast, that the watrines be clean gotten out,
ether by a lebek, (with a nose) or a blind lembek, whose nether skirt have a
hollow gutter or circle ether by it self, or with waters convenient for every
disease. This oil I have tasted my self, it is swiet, pleasant, and strong, in
colour (if I remember well) somewhat white.

An other way. Take.iiii. pounds of Vitriol of Rome, dry it in an earthen
vessel till it wax red, after when it is beaten put it into a belly of glass
diligently defenced with clay (as the manner is for Aqua fortis) and first
destilit with a soft fire, encresing the degre of the fire by little and little,
until Acetosae, somewhat warm, putting unto it half a dram of spices
Diamargariton, which is cold if it may be gotten.

An other way to make oil of Vitriol against in rabble diseases. Put as much
Vitriol of Rome as ye will in a belly to wax red, with such a fire as is used to
Aqua fortis, for ye space of.xxiiii. hours, as loge as the water comes forth
without spirits, and more if it be not made red, ever kepinge the same fire.
When as it is now becomed red, take away ye head (lembek) and the receiver, and
keep the water for secret uses to be spoken of. After beat ye Vitriol and put
it in a belly with.v. parts of quintessece of wine, that the Vitriol may be
soked: The belly Aqua fortis is made. So shall run out first the Aqua vitae, and
at length the fire increased, oil of Vitriol shall follow. Then thou shalt
separate the Aqua vitae from the oil, putting a head to the belly wherein both are
contained, setting a receiver without, with a fire of Aqua fortis. morning, and
forbid them to receive any meet before.iiii. hours be past. Against a cotinual
ague give.viii. drops, with half an uncle of Rose water, in the morning as is
said and likewise also against other diseases, Dosin, that is the quantity of
the receipt, unto strong men thou may give.viii. drops, to men of men
strength five, to such as be weak iiii. c. In this oyll if thou dissolve
Marchasit, it shall change silver, and tinge it in all degries.

An other way for the same, that it may be the Crucibulorum glased within as
much Vitrioll of Rome as thou wilt: and destill it in a fornace, as is before
said, with a fire of Aqua fortis and there shall run out a white water of
Vitriol: After when it cease, thou shalt increase the fire, and a grien water
shall follow, which when it hath left thou shalt make a most strong and vehement
fire, both above and beneth, and a red oil shall issue out. Change ever the
receiver according to liquors in one vessel, seperate the waters afterward from
the oil by destilling them, and the oyll shall remain in the belly. This
separatio is made ye belly stading upright (with a head and a receiver) the
first destillacion of ye oil, the belly lying ouerth warth, as it is said. If
thou dip a little dry woul or bombase in water of Vitriol of Rome, and there with
thouch any kind of diseases of ye mouth, thou shalt easily heal them: Out of a
written book of a certain friend: he seems here to mean that water yt
Vitriol, which is more precious and pure, and is kept to be ministered given to
drink against inward diseases.

Of the virtues of oil of Vitriol, out of ye same written book. Drink Malmsy
with a little oyll of Vitriol, continually for the space of.v. or.viii. dais, it
riddeth a man from all obstructions, it purges the blood, and drives away the
stone. It heals the il scab, if it be drunk with water of fumitory,
Myrobalana condite. It renews a ma with water of endiue. It heals all manner
of griefs of the head, with water of Maioram, or Buglos, or Melissa: also the
turnsicknes, if it be contained any space. With water of Agresta it heals al
manner of diseases, the body being first purged. It restores the memory with
the water of Acorus or Fenell. It mouith a man to sleep, with the sied of Letis
or Popy. It is good for melancolyck persons with water of Bublos or Borage. It
cures with water of wyld few. It purges the body with Aqua vitae. It heals
ye palsy with water of wyld mint, or sage, Hyssop, the cramp with water of
Sage: the sickness of quaking with water of Basilicus, diverse inward diseases
with water of Trifolium, all feblenes of the eyes with water of Fenell: the
reum from the head with water of Lily, ye catar with water of Adiantu Hyssop, the
cough, also the disease of the side with water of Platain the Pleuresis with
water of maiden hear, the feblenes Diarhodon. It stints ye flux of the belly
with the water of Plantain: the co lyck with water of Few. With water of
wormwod it resistith venomous bytings. It heals al manner of impostumes and
dropsy, continuing it. It is good for the limes that be resolved, if it be
Tamarindis: with water of Radish and and sea bremble, it expels the stoone,
opens the stoppinges of theines. It heals all agues with water of Agresta,
certain kinds of leprosy, cotinuing the use of it. This is the true potable
gold, and the true Seladyn or Chelidonia, more also in weigth it gives not
place to gold, it hath the same as many virtues as potable gould. A little of it
with a little water of Roses drunk, restores ye

An other manner of oyll of Vitriol, which a certain old man a practicioner in
Heluetia used, mixting.ii. or.iii. drops with Triacle, and bidding the to sweet
after they had drunk it, in a bed.iiii. or. v hours, so that they put not out
so much as a fingar, by the which medicine I know many too be cured of him
from diseases hard to be cured. c. When he died I saw the oyll which me
thougth was of somewhat a white colour or duskish, perauenture because of the
little pieces of silver that Vitriol, or as much as ye list in a large earthen
vessel glased, and fenced without every where roud Vitriol many enough from
above in the very vessel, and leave it so till the Vitriol be clean brought to
lime, that no moisture or vapor at all remain in it, and that now it have
gotten a redish or yelowish colour, nor any vapour or spirits seem to ascend
from it any more. For except ye Vitriol be very dry, oil effectual strong
enough should not be drawn out of it, but mixed with a certain white fleum. When
as therefore it is sufficiently brought into lime, put away the fire, and
when the vessel is couled by little and little, take Vitriol as well as ye ca
with a knife or otherwise: although it is no harde matter to get it out of a
glased vessel. The Vitriol take out, break it small, put the pieces into an
erthen belly, which the potter, as be spoken, hath made of ye best earth, and
wonderfully well baked, so strong that it my be able to abide a vehement fire
in a with clay, and yt, ii. or.iii. fold, yt is, first dried parieted again,
again. The form of the fornace shall be in this sort. This fornace shall be
butlded. 4 square, in the top a little imbosed vaulted roud in the midst of ye
top of ye arch shall be made a hole or smoking vent, so large, y^ every hour or as
oft as nead shall require, coals may be put conveniently into ye fornace by it,
with a log iron fire shouel, to put in the coals getlely charily wtall yt they
may slide down about the belly in such wise yt it be not hurt. In the. 4.
corners also above must be left holes or spirits should brethe out. This clai
must be suffered to be dried, before ye begin the business. Moreover there must
yet.ii. holes be made in the ii. contrary sides of the fornace (not in yt side
yt the belly looks out at, nether in the contrary, but in the other two. These
also must have their stopples to shut the with al, yt the heat may be kept in.
The use of these holes, yt the coals which are put in at the top of ye valt may
be hadsoly disposed with some iron prog for the purpose put in at ye holes,
ordered in such wise yt his full strength, and this is a token of perfection.
Therefore thou shalt let the fire to go out and the fornace once couled, take
away the receiver, and turning it in thy hands, and inclining it now to one
side, now to an other, gather all the drops together that cleue unto the sides,
and the oil or liquor so gathered, pour it into a vessel of the best Venice
glass: for it is danger least the commun glass should be eaten through of it,
for it consumes and eteth like Aqua fortis, This liquor that practicioner
Haganovv perauenture, or Colen or Acon: for there men say the best and
strongest

Of the burning or broylinge of Chalcanthum, that is Vitriol, and his kinds.
Bulcasis, writes in a manner the same things in his third book of the
preparation of medicines, which we have declared afoore in his preparation for
the making of Vitriol Zimor, also he teaches to prepare after the same manner.
But amongst diverse ways of this oil of Vitriol, I like that best which I
described last. For the liquor that is destilled that way is the sharpest of
all, and also the tartest, in so much that it may be called vinegar of metal,
as me thinks: Wherefore of certain it is highly commended for the quenshing of
thirst in somer time, one drop of it put into a draught of wine, like as I
found in a certain doutch writ book, where as this also is added: Vitriolum
is

An other way out of the same book. Stiep Vitriol in Aqua fortis, which may

fortis by destillacion, an oyll shall remain. But perauentur this way is to
dangerous that a liquor so destilled should be received within the body. But

I remember I have red in sum place in Lulli{us} in his work of Quintessence,
where he makes mecion of oil or Quintessence of Vitriol. But in what sort it
should be made, I could never yet find in any book that went abroad: so
greatly have they all kept secret this thing as a marvelous mystery. For the
description which I will declare here after out of the book of Nicolas Massa
upon the disease of Naples, can not be received within ye body.

When the Chalcanthum, that is the Vitriol, or Mysis that is Vitriol of Rome is
brent an oyll most sharp hot is drawn out of it by the force of the fire, in
vessels of glass wherewith if a man touche wartes when they are cut or wounded,
they will go away. The same if a ma taste it, it strikes the tong like as it
were a hot iron. Yet the use of it is to dry boils within that be out of hoop
of recovery, where as they be not much filthy, as it chances in certain that be
diseased of Phthoe corrupcion matter without grief. It serves also to cut
Cardanus. The same coniectur we write before, that oil of Mysis or arsnick
anointed without may seem to deliver fro poyso. The spirit or Quintesseuce of
Vitriol is praised of certain practicioners against the falling sickness and
Apoplexia or benumbing of senses.

Shomakers inck lowseth the belly, both in honey and meed drunk to the weight of
a dram, also in wine, specially the oyll thereof. George Agricola, Vitriol doth
kill not only men but tries: wherefore it must be made in sum out syd or place
where no man dwells. Albucasis other show the way of making it, Brassauolus
(In mine opinion not the oil, but ye smoke of Vitriol while it is brent with
fire prepared unto destillacio is so hurtful.) And again, of Chalcanthu, yt is
vitriol oil is made so burning, that we use it for potetiall fire: for it is of
a caustical, you is a burning nature, with a knief anoited with Olives. While
ye oylis preparing, ye must take heed of the smoke: because it doth not only
kyl men but also the tries that be ny, it dries the up. The trial whereof
Fraciscus de Mote the notable bone setter whose tries of his archard every one
died with the smoke of Vitriol while he prepared the oyll thereof.

The oil of Vitriol is marvelous, burning like a hot iro without grief, is
made in this manner, xxx. vnces of Vitriol of Rome or of Cypres, Salnitrum,
Bocia clayed for the fire of an alchemists fornace, and by the fire thou shalt
have the oil incresed in the receiver: which is a marvelous Cauterium or
burning thing, and hath no pere in any operation, and chiefly in taking away of
wens great wartes. But the receiver must be great, if thou wilt make the
forsaid oil: Nicolas Massa in Naples, and Thomas Philologus, who takes.xx.
drames of Vitriol, but of Alum and salt of ether. xxiiii A water of diverse
metals (out of a certain dutch book) for the leprosi, spots dunnes of the eyes.
The filing of silver coper, stiele, gould, of every one as much as ye can
get: the first day put it in vryn while it is warm made by a boy or wench
that is a maid, the next day in the crumbs of hot bread: the third in a white
of an egg: the fourth in the milk of a Then put all this into a still
destill them with a little fire, and kip it. For the virtue of it is
incomparable. It is good against the leprosy, and al the spots in the face, and
it procures unto the face a youthful brightness, it makes also clearness of ye
sight this shalt thou reed otherwise in the Addicions upon the Breuiarium or
Bridgment of Arnold de Villa Nona. 1. 18.

Of Aqua fortis and such like.
E described a little before a certain water like Aqua fortis, destilled of
Vitriol, Sal Nitrum, and Alum against great wartes. c. But the commun Aqua
fortis also, and the simple oil of Vitriol, if a man put a drop of them in to a
wen or wart first cut, they take it away: of the which thing I made a trial
in my self upon a sied wart on my fyngars end, whereinto when I had first cut
it with a razer, I Aqua fortis, and although it wet not away by by, yet within
a few weeks is was gon Aqua fortis or to separate metalles is thus made. One
part of Sal nitrum, liquid or molten Alum (that they call roche.iii. parts:
sand half a part, when they are dried diligently and purged with the fire, let
them be destilled in a vessel of glass. It is gathered by it self, that which
issues out first, at length when the glass looks like a safro colour,
increase the fire and an other follows: and yet if thou take it in water of
the fountain or well, it is yet so sharpe that never the les it dissolveth
silver, and separateth it from Goulde. It is separated in this wise. Take a
little quantity of ye water drawn out, and put into it the weight of. xii grains
of very pure silver* and set it upon ashes till the silver be dissolved. This
shall send down into the bottom of the vessel, grounds like unto fine lime,
which taken away the pure water that remains, put it to the hole water from
the which Aqua fortis but of another manner of making.) But seeing it vanishes
away easili and consumes, it shall be kept in a glass diligently shut. To a man
that imagines how great strengthes it hath, which taking Ammoniak and Nitrum,
with Chalcanthum (yt is coproos) and Alum molten in equal porcions, putting
unto them at last one fourth part of roust: this made It yet a man ad and put
to a little of the obstracite stone, called Smiris wherewith they polish
precious stones, thou shalt have more plenty of water and better, because it
will not be burned. These things therefore received and found true by trials,
let us see what should be cause that this water becomes so strong: for
manifest experience teaches, that the drier part attenuated and fined by the
force of the fire, receives a firye and a fretting or gnawing strength. But
why burns not Chalcanthum by the force of the fire, for as much as it
turns the driest part into humour, it is most sharpe, and strikes the tongue
like fire. Cardan. Let no manne think that this liquor perteineth Chalcanthum
or Coproos an ounce of Aqua fortis: mixed it with an ounce and a half of
Roosewater, soores of the throat, palace, jaws and lips, let them be touched
twice a day with a little Cotton tide to the top of a stick and moistened in
this liquor: Thom. Philologus.

A water to whitten the teeth which Isabella of Arragonia, the Duchess of
Millen did use. A pound of Salt purged and beaten: an ounce of Gla^sye or Isly
Alum, let them be destilled in a lembecke, Mixed an ounce of this water with an
uncle of Plantaine water, and with a little wode wouldipte therein rub the
teethe, and they shall become Furnerius.

An other like out of the same book. Sall Ammo niak, Sall Gemmae of ether. iii
ounces, Sugar Alum an ounce and a half, commone Salt, an ounce. When they are
beaten destil them in a lembecke of glass: and with the liquor drawn out
thereof rub the teeth with a stone, and after wash the mouth with a little white
wine. Read before in the end of the Cosmeticall waters, the same description,
but without common salt, the use whereof is declared without destillacion.

Aqua Angelica of a marvelous virtue against blearednesse, Cankar, and burning
with fire. Three ounces of vn^lekt lime and half a pound of rain water, let
them stand together in a vessel of glass or tin a.iii. days. Then
mirtinge them stir them together, and let them settle again a.xxiii. hours or
more in a vessel well covered. Afterward strain them tenderly through a
linen clothe till it be clear. Then put to it.x. drawmes of Sall Ammoniak
the whitest thou cast Filtrum. This water heals the clothe or spot (La Toil
in French, that is the web) of the eyes, three drops thrice a day dropped
into them, continuing till the eye be made whole. It takes away also the
tears of the eyes, the redness and blearednesse, also the Cankar and burning
if it be rightly steines of cloth both silk and woullen, if they be washed in
it a little warmed. Furnerius.

A way to make red powder, yt is quicksiluer calcionated precipitated, out of
Marianus ye surgeo. Aqua fortis. iiii. vnces of quicksiluer, mixed the together
in a belly or cucurbita of glass well claied, with a head upon it, y^ nose end
whereof shall be put within a receiver, let them be destilled with a moderat
fire (increasing it by little little. But aqua fortis that separateth gold fro
silver is made thus. Sal nitru, roche Alu, Vitriol of Rome, of eve ry one.ii.
poudes: let the be mixed in a mortar, ever beating grinding with the pestil till
they be well mixed. Then put the powder somewhat groos into a Praecipitatu an
uncle a half, rosed honey.ii. vnces, mixed them diligently. With this medicine
without doubt thou shalt dry clese a filthy sore and roten (wherupo the flesh
shall after begin to breed) where as other clensing things, as those made of ye
juice Apiu, or of ye juice of Cynoglos shall do no good.

Nicolas Massa in his book of the French disease, calls Mercurium
praecipitatum, Angelical powder, because of the marvelous as it were a divine
operation of it in the Frech pockes, which he his self hath not seldom tried.
This medicin (saith he) dries, with a certain gentle eating of the soft and
superfluous flesh, and that without grief, removing also the evil secret
quality of the soores, and chiefly of the disease of Naples. It digests any
matter, and purges it, lets the Corrosio of gnawyng the canker: it
dissolveth groos matter, hard and raw, after ye opening of gummes. And no
medicine is to be compared with this in this disease. For if thou continue in
the use of it, it leads unto the perfect breding of the skin, as I have
oftentimes tried: and it is excellent in the evil sores of the yard. It is
made in this wise. But a pound of quick silver in a little belly of glass, and
power as much Aqua fortis unto it. Then put the belly in a pot and ashes in
Mercurium calcionated red. Grynde this, if any part of the quick silver
remain with it, put the said powder in a cleen vessel of bras at the fire, be
consumed. This powder may thou use to all the forsaid diseases and specially
to the sores of the yard, of other places, where rottennes and much il matter
lets the knitting or heling up: and in fistulaes dissolve it with wine, and
cast it in by a brazen pipe, for it works marvelously.

Moreover water to separate gold from silver is thus made. Two pounds of
Vitriol of Rome Roche Alum.xvi. ounces: Sal Nitrum a pound: let them be put in
a crooked belly (writhe backward)

But this angelical powder had I of a certain old Alcumist, and I made it
before Iohannes de Vigo ever made any mention of it. Thus far Massa: and
part Thom. Philologus out of him.

Of the making and commodities of this red powder, read Iohannes de Vigo in
his fifte book of Additionum: where he bids that the vessels rereceiuer
shall be thrice as big as the bealye, the xxxviii. leaf. b. And that white
found with this powder, is silver sublimated from the red: like as is what so
ever is yelowe or of a Saffron colour. And also in his book entitled
Capiosa, the. Clxiii. lefe. a.

Powder of Mercury (saith Matthaeolus Senensis, in his book of the way to
heal the French disease) is made in this manner. Take.iiii. pouds of water,
wherewith gould is separated from silver: Acetosae, of ether ii. ounces, the
next morrow early take the waters from thence and put new unto it, and set it to
the fire in a vessel of bras or earth: when they are hot, cease not to stur them
about with an iron or woden spattle or s^is until al become powder and that
when thou list make such a recept against ye french disease as well that is
Flegmatike as Melancholy. Take electuarii Conciliatoris (this is made of diverse
cordial medicines, and spices, precious stones, pearls, gould, silver,
Camphora, Ambra, Mosch: is described of him, Differentia. 196) half a scruple,
perls, hyacincts, of ether.v. grains: the powder of Praecipitatum. v. grains:
powder of D^amuscum, Diamargariton, of ether half a scrupull: Make.v. pills
(let the be gilded, Thom, Philolog{us} Terrae Sigillatae and Boli Armeniae of
every.iii. grains,) let these be taken of the paciet an hour before day: let
him keep his bed.v. hours. Shortly, believe me, shall the french pocks be
avoided with this receipt. For the fleum and blak choler also shall vanish away
both by vomit and downwards. Besides this there are very many kinds of
diseases that we have cured with such a powder. For it puts not away only
matter and rotten flesh being strawed upon, but also without Tuneci, which
they call Carduum Benedictum, or with an electuarye of precious stones, if it be
not yet confirmed stablished in the body, it drives it away meruelouslye.
Many also that be Limphatici, that is, mad, or Melancolike, whom they
believed commonly to be resorted unto of Devils, we have cured them with ye
same. What make I mani words almost dead of the quartain, putting unto it
Saccharum Buglossatum or triacle, or Mithridatium, some digestion made, an hour
before the fit, in.v. or vii. grains weight, according to the age and streght
of the body of the diseased. Yea also it is holso to be ministered amongst the
griefs of the yard great guts: for we have cured some that avoided their dung
by their mouth: leaning to the moniments and sayings of Paulus Aegineta, that
saith, how certain phisitios have ministered in that disease Athesin, did
prepare Mercurium praecipitatum with gould, and sold it like gold, which had
such virtue, to eat out gnawinge or grief. Se those that we shall declare
about the end of those that follow next after.

How Praecipitatum is made, which is a remedy against all diseases growing of
the rottennes of humours, out of a certain write book. Make a water of equal
porcions of Vitriol of Rome and Sal Nitrum, with a head and receiver, in the
which thou shalt put the sixt-part of the weighte of raw Mercury, yt is to
say, if there be. 3. pouds of Vitriol and Sal nitrum, put.vi. vnces of Mercury.
Afterward suffer the water with his spirits to descend in to the receiver.
Then avoid all that is in the receiver into a clean belly and that is claied:
under the which put a head with a receiver, and destill it again: and when the
water is in the receiver, put it again in the belly in the which the Mercury
remained. Thou shalt repeat this till the Mercury wax red. Then when it is red
wash it with Cordial waters, as Borage Balm and such like. Mercury so
prepared shalt thou give to sick men within their bodies, in this manner. If the
body be very strong, give.x. grains if it be mean.viii. weakes, five: if it be
a child, consider diligently what is necessary to be done. But utterly mixed it
with triacle: so shalt thou give it to him that is infected with poison,
droysy, pestilece or taken with other infirmity. If a sound man once a year,
or every third year, as it shall seem Praecipitatum with a dew digestion of
the humours, that is with a preparation of purgation, he shall prevent many
diseases. Note that in the stead of Mercury thou may use Amal gama made of
six parts of quick silver and of one part of gold and so shalt thou work
greatter woders. (This Amalgam must be made red like as Mercury alone with
Aqua fortis: although Mattheolus Senensis, as we declared a little before, wry
teeth that the powder Mercurial may be made of Aqua fortis.) And mark that
thou may heal wounds with the first or second Praecipitatum, which thou
shalt use thus: Put of it about the wound and within. And this is a great
secret. And know that in.iiii. destillacions thou shalt bring this to pas:
which done, put it in a clean belly in the fire, that the spirits (that is
of the Hydrargyri that is the quick silver sublimated mixed with the
Praecipitatum) as much as is possible may depart, then make as is above
specified.

Of the sublimacion of quick silver, thou shalt read Bulcasis in his third
book of his work that he calls Servitor. But of the use of it in burninges
and seerynges, and for the French disease, read Nicolaus Massa the sixte book,
the second chapter, and of the same book the fourth, howe it is to be ordered
to seerynges, both otherwise, and that the seeryng or burning be done with none
or little grief. Certain use it at this day for the ill and angry skabes, and
ring worms or tettares. c.

Quick silver (says Cardan) is sublimated in this manner. Put Quick silver and
Shomakers inck of ether like weight, and with most sharpe white vynegar mixed
it so long, till the quick silver be seen no more: then in a vessel of glass
parieted with clay sis it till it grow together. If any do run abroad cum
not together, break it again in a mortar with vinegar put to it, and sis it
yet again. They use quick silver so excoct for painting faces. But it makes
the ties fall out and briedeth a stinking breath. But for the use of silver and
for the art of Goldsmythes, it is proffitable not in few things. Of the
sublimation of Mercury, Marchasyt, Magnesiae, Tutiae, look in Geber Summae
perfectionis, 1. 4. 45. and so furth. Also of the sublimacion of Brimstone and
arsnick. 43. chapter. Sublimatum, Praecipitatum, and Cinabrium are dissolved
with strong vinegar, specially destilled, and return into quic silver.
Syluius.

It hath the nature of Brymstone in heating and drying. Being calcinated with
the fire it waxes black, and by and by with sublimation it becummeth most
white. If it be sublimated three or four times it purchases such strength,
that it will

Salt that it may be more pure to be put to medicines or meates, after it is
mixed with water let it be destilled by a Filtrum, and again let it be sod till
the water be consumed. The same purged in a gouldsmithes Crucibulo with a
great fire is molten and fused. When it is so molten, let it be mixed with
Salt Alcalis (or in stead of it with the white gall of glass (for there is
black also) which some call the norishmente of glass, other Zoza as Sal Gemmae.
When these are beaten they use them for Chrysocolla, or also they put a little
of Chrysocolla unto it. But this mixture hath to much sharpnes, and consumes
some of ye gold. Wherefore they use it only to courser works, but to finer they
use only Borax. There be so that mixed Borax, commun salt molten and salt
Alcalis together in equal porcions, and in secret matters count it for
Borax. But these are besides the matters perteining to physic.
